  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b29f42f0-1c6e-4803-a71f-dd5fe4384788'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer3859331877078348089">Ruthless and supremely powerful, the Great Library is now a presence in every major city, governing the flow of knowledge to the masses.   <span id="freeText3859331877078348089" style="display:none">Ruthless and supremely powerful, the Great Library is now a presence in every major city, governing the flow of knowledge to the masses. Alchemy allows the Library to deliver the content of the greatest works of history instantly—but the personal ownership of books is expressly forbidden.<br /> <br />Jess Brightwell believes in the value of the Library, but the majority of his knowledge comes from illegal books obtained by his family, who are involved in the thriving black market. Jess has been sent to be his family’s spy, but his loyalties are tested in the final months of his training to enter the Library’s service.<br /> <br />When his friend inadvertently commits heresy by creating a device that could change the world, Jess discovers that those who control the Great Library believe that knowledge is more valuable than any human life—and soon both heretics and books will burn…</span>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/600851-deann">DeAnn</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I would recommend it for kids 12 and above, but, if you happen to have a bookish 10 year old who is emotionally more mature that his or her age, I wou<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I would recommend it for kids 12 and above, but, if you happen to have a bookish 10 year old who is emotionally more mature that his or her age, I wouldn't turn them away from reading it. It's really kind of a combination of Harry Potter and Hunger Games and Steampunk in a library setting. There is violence and war and the horrors that go with that, but the author doesn't dwell on it. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div id="review_1130200056" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1130200056" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1130200056?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=paranormal-uf">paranormal-uf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1130200056" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17997583546302714516"><b>
  <i>"We're nothing but secrets."</i>
</b><br/><br/>Books, alchemy, secret tunnels, books, friendships, rivalries, books and villains who become heroes? Oh, and did I mention books? Oh so many books...<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1436568043ra/15478826.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I might complain every time I read that ridiculous "X meets Y" marketing strategy, but I have to admit that <i>Harry Potter</i> meets <i>The Book Thief</i> meets <i>Fahrenheit 451</i> is a pretty good descriptor for this book. The main character - Jess - is indeed a book thief, and they're are people called Burners who (you guessed it!) b</span>
  <span id="freeText17997583546302714516" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"We're nothing but secrets."</i>
</b><br><br>Books, alchemy, secret tunnels, books, friendships, rivalries, books and villains who become heroes? Oh, and did I mention books? Oh so many books...<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1436568043ra/15478826.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I might complain every time I read that ridiculous "X meets Y" marketing strategy, but I have to admit that <i>Harry Potter</i> meets <i>The Book Thief</i> meets <i>Fahrenheit 451</i> is a pretty good descriptor for this book. The main character - Jess - is indeed a book thief, and they're are people called Burners who (you guessed it!) burn books for political protest in this alternate world where the Great Library rules.<br><br><i>
  <b>"The truth was what the library wanted it to be."</b>
</i><br><br>So you might be wondering where the Harry Potter part comes in. Well, let's imagine for a second that HP wasn't so much about wizards as it was about alchemists, and that Harry didn't go to Hogwarts but instead went to The Great Library in Alexandria, Egypt. Where there are teachers who may or may not be evil, leaders who almost certainly can't be trusted, and all the friendships and rivalries you would expect from teenagers competing to be scholars.<br><br>I can't say it's a perfect book, <b>but it is damn entertaining.</b> From the beautiful descriptions of Alexandria, to the frightening presence of the Library's leaders; from the competition, to the importance of friendship and the mix of funny and touching friendship dynamics. Everyone has secrets and the "bad guys" might not be what you first expect.<br><br>After this wonderful, diverse cast of characters, my favourite thing has to be the books. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20643052.Ink_and_Bone__The_Great_Library___1_" title="Ink and Bone (The Great Library, #1) by Rachel Caine" rel="nofollow noopener">Ink and Bone</a> is about love for books, the power of books, the lengths people will go to for books. Also, though this may be unintentional, I got a sense of an underlying symbolism about the difference between ebooks and physical books in our world. Ebooks are convenient, more universal, I read them all the time... but does anything ever really compare to having the physical ink and paper in your hands?<br><br><b>A fast-paced, exciting read</b>. No cliffhanger, but perfectly set up for the sequel. I can't wait!<br><br>Edit: And, just in case you were wondering, I didn't like the <i>Morganville Vampires</i> series and that had no bearing on my enjoyment of this.<br><br><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://mycountryheart.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCcVsMUSAzMlIKs3nw-xe_nw" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17997583546302714516" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1352973776" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1352973776" />
    <a title="Felicia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/666892-felicia"><img alt="Felicia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1437521850p2/666892.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1352973776?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Felicia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Felicia" href="/user/show/666892-felicia">Felicia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/666892-felicia?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/666892-felicia?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1352973776" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3263186729068480476">I am on book tour currently, and now appreciate every author who ever lived because this stuff is CRAY! It's like doing a convention for 3 weeks straight, but you're flying to different cities every day and since i'm a REALLY picky sleeper, I'm starting to feel like someone's trying to murder me if the bed has a low thread count. Anyway, I loaded my Kindle up with reads in anticipation of traveling a lot, and this book was #1 on my list to get to first. And I loved it!<br/><br/>I'm a big fan of Rachel Cai</span>
  <span id="freeText3263186729068480476" style="display:none">I am on book tour currently, and now appreciate every author who ever lived because this stuff is CRAY! It's like doing a convention for 3 weeks straight, but you're flying to different cities every day and since i'm a REALLY picky sleeper, I'm starting to feel like someone's trying to murder me if the bed has a low thread count. Anyway, I loaded my Kindle up with reads in anticipation of traveling a lot, and this book was #1 on my list to get to first. And I loved it!<br /><br />I'm a big fan of Rachel Caine from her romance novels (and I know her in real life because I fanned out when I met her over her books several years ago, haha). She wrote a few series we've read in my Vaginal Fantasy book club, so imagine my surprise when I read this, and it's not a girlie romance at all, it's a YA novel with a boy protagonist. And it's SO GOOD! <br /><br />This series is a fantasy love letter to books. When I was reading it, all I could think about was how much I loved going into a library as a kid and flipping through the books and finding new worlds. How it was forbidden to draw in a book and how terrible it was to mess one up in the slightest. Books were special. This series is set in an alt world where printing presses don't exist, the Library in Alexandria never was burnt, and knowledge is controlled by an all-powerful Library (capital letter). Our hero is a member of a family who smuggles actual books, so you're dropped immediately into a fantasy world that's rich with conflict. Anyway, I don't want to give more away, but there are amazing themes about freedom and the average person's right to knowledge, as well as the permeating feeling of REVERENCE towards books. I felt very guilty that I was reading it on a kindle, lol, and wanted to run out and buy a real live book immediately after reading. <br /><br />Anyway, if you love books, this is a great read. It's YA in tone but not too kiddie, there's some dramatic stuff that happens, but it sets up for some great twists in the next book, which I'll be sure to pick up. A quick fun read. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3263186729068480476" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1372683206" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1372683206" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1372683206?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=books-about-books">books-about-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1372683206" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12505679752977447179"><br/><b>Phew! What a journey this book was!</b> I’ve read ‘‘books about books’’ before, but nothing comparable to this one. I presently have a great deal of emotions inside me because of this story and, really, I had no idea that this author would be so ruthless! You have no clue how many people die, how many deceptions and manipulations occur. It was a journey because, when you look at the first and last chapters, you realize how much happened, how much changed and how things will never be how they were be</span>
  <span id="freeText12505679752977447179" style="display:none"><br /><b>Phew! What a journey this book was!</b> I’ve read ‘‘books about books’’ before, but nothing comparable to this one. I presently have a great deal of emotions inside me because of this story and, really, I had no idea that this author would be so ruthless! You have no clue how many people die, how many deceptions and manipulations occur. It was a journey because, when you look at the first and last chapters, you realize how much happened, how much changed and how things will never be how they were before.<br /><br /><b>The beginning was lent, extremely so.</b> I almost regretted buying the hardcover after reading the first chapters. The writing felt so methodical and I simply couldn’t find it in myself to care for anyone. Jess lives in a family of book smugglers which, when you think about it, looks pretty darn interesting. For me, things got <i>truly</i> interesting when he got admitted to this special school to study the library and its elements (something I had no idea would happen before starting it – can I just mention that I love delightful surprises and boarding schools?) A very delightful surprise indeed as we met plenty of new characters with unique personalities. From that moment, characters (Jess mostly) stopped feeling one-dimensional and I stopped thinking of the writing as being extremely methodical.<br /><br />Jess was a character who didn’t share much about himself. Since this story was narrated in the third person, you can imagine how that made it difficult to connect or warm up to him. Luckily, him being the hero, after a while you get used to his introverted self and can definitely guess what his feelings can be toward whatever person or situation, since they were rarely thoroughly described, detailed. My favorite characters turned out to be Wolfe and Santi who are both mentors (well, the first is and the second always assisting him). This hopefully doesn’t come as a surprise if you know in the slightest bit how I love my characters to be - but you’ll understand better when reading. I’m only going to say—yay diversity!<br /><br />Even if you don’t end up caring too evidently about the characters or may guess that you wouldn’t, it’s still worth reading if only to take a dive into the world-building which, I have to say, was completely engrossing. I bet you’ll want to swim for a little while in it. Writing this review, I keep thinking of the fact that the next instalment will be in my hands in about a year and I’m truthfully sad because I really, really came to love so much about this series. Even the Harry Potter similarities (there were a tiny few) didn’t bother me in the end, although they struck me during my reading.<br /><br /><b>A solid book.</b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12505679752977447179" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2368295080" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2368295080" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2368295080?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=received-to-review">received-to-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=berkleypub">berkleypub</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2368295080" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16595156378450406566"><blockquote>
  <i>You have ink in your blood, boy, and no help for it. Books will never be just a business to you.</i>
  <br/>
  <br/>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529208383i/25805301._SY540_.jpg' width='375' height='375' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</blockquote> Few people, if any, have ever <b>set eyes on a book</b> in Jess Brightwell's London. And yet, <b>no one is illiterate</b> and writing is considered sacred across the world.<br/><br/>Instead of books, <b>everyone has blanks</b> (think: ereader but run by alchemy and magic) where they can rent as many books as they want, respond to messages and conduct their lessons on. <br/><br/>But no one has a book - as in an actual printed bo</span>
  <span id="freeText16595156378450406566" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>You have ink in your blood, boy, and no help for it. Books will never be just a business to you.</i>
  <br>
  <br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529208383i/25805301._SY540_.jpg" width="375" height="375" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote> Few people, if any, have ever <b>set eyes on a book</b> in Jess Brightwell's London. And yet, <b>no one is illiterate</b> and writing is considered sacred across the world.<br><br>Instead of books, <b>everyone has blanks</b> (think: ereader but run by alchemy and magic) where they can rent as many books as they want, respond to messages and conduct their lessons on. <br><br>But no one has a book - as in an actual printed book -<b> because having one is punishable by death.</b><br><br>Jess Brightwell and his family are book-smugglers. They find printed copies of books and sell them to the highest bidder. And if they get caught - <b>they will hang</b>.<br><br>Jess father decides he wants <b>an inside man. </b>Someone who could have access to the handwritten texts of the greats and who could influence the right people to turn a blind eye. <br><br>And so, Jess is going to apply for one of the<b> most dangerous, grueling and brutal</b> jobs in the world. He's going to become a <b>
  <i>Librarian.</i>
</b><blockquote>
  <i>The first purpose of a librarian is to preserve and defend our books. Sometimes, that means dying for them - or making someone else die for them. </i>
</blockquote><b>The Great Library of Alexandria </b> has spread its tendrils in every major country. It promotes literacy while keeping the population in check. <blockquote>
  <i>The Great Library may have once been a boon, but what is it today? What does it give us? It suppresses! It stifles! </i>
</blockquote> Jess and 30 other students from across the world compete for six librarian spots. Quickly, they realize that this will be no picnic.<br><br>Anyone can be sent home at any time. And Jess is learning that the world isn't quite as stable as the Great Library wants them to think.<br><br>Jess is fairly confident he can make it...but the longer he stays, the more he realizes that he has no idea of <b>how (or even if) he can ever get out.</b><br><br><b>What a brilliant start to a series!</b><br><br>It's so rare to get a <b>YA series with a male lead </b>- this entire book was a breath of fresh air. Jess was down-to-earth, entertaining and absolutely endearing. Watching his struggle as he transitions from a scared kid to a bold survivor definitely kept me hooked.<br><br>I'm also so impressed by<b> Caine's world-building. </b>She took such a fundamental concept (the printed word) and built a society around its absence.<br><br> I was thoroughly fascinated by how she just took this idea and ran with it (though, as a huge library lover, I did have a really difficult time associating anything negative with libraries).<br><br>Overall, I cannot wait to read what she writes next!<br><br><i>With thanks to Berkley Publishing for sending me a free copy in exchange for an honest review.</i><br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br><br>Happy Reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16595156378450406566" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1162732109" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1162732109" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1162732109?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=steampunk">steampunk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=magical-fantasy">magical-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=ya-male-narrators">ya-male-narrators</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1162732109" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5008523978187659338"><b>REREAD: June 2017</b><br/><br/>Because I remember NOTHING I decided to reread this before heading onwards with the series. <b>And omg I'm so glad I did.</b> This book is precious and so book-loving and the appreciation for novels is just giving me life. I <i>nearly</i> up it to 5-stars, but the romance still annoys me. #Alas.<br/><br/>Also fyi the audiobook is <i>incredible</i>. The narrator is British and Jess' London accent is my favourite thing. The narrator puts so so much emotion into it, it just made the book come really alive! Plus </span>
  <span id="freeText5008523978187659338" style="display:none"><b>REREAD: June 2017</b><br /><br />Because I remember NOTHING I decided to reread this before heading onwards with the series. <b>And omg I'm so glad I did.</b> This book is precious and so book-loving and the appreciation for novels is just giving me life. I <i>nearly</i> up it to 5-stars, but the romance still annoys me. #Alas.<br /><br />Also fyi the audiobook is <i>incredible</i>. The narrator is British and Jess' London accent is my favourite thing. The narrator puts so so much emotion into it, it just made the book come really alive! Plus Wolfe has a Scottish accent and I'm 5000% a fan.<br /><br /><b>Quick Bucket Of New(ish) Thoughts:</b><br />• Jess is actually adorable and my favourite.<br />• I still wish we knew more about Brendan!!<br />• THE LEVEL OF BOOK LOVING IS AMAZING. Like Jess is traumatised from seeing someone eat a book.<br />• Same, son, same.<br />• I still don't really understand the entire magic system??<br />• The library sucks, man.<br />• Wolfe x Santi are the ultimate ship in this book.<br />• I still am peeved at how Jess gets so consumed with Morgan that he packs up his brain into a hollow bucket and posts it to Guadeloupe. I mean. Mate. Focus here.<br />• Morgan is also like one foot in the manic pixie dream girl grave.<br />• KAHLEELAAAAAAA. She wears a hijab and is the smartest and also the best. &lt;3<br />• I find it ironic how opposed to "fake" books this is, and like I'm legit sitting here listening to an audio instead of an actual physical copy. HA.<br />• I forgot what Thomas did for Jess at the end. hoLD me I'm crying.<br />• i HAVE SO MANY EMOTIONS.<br />• I REALLY LOVE THIS BOOK.<br />• DARK PSYCHO LIBRARY SYSTEMS. Bring me the sequel.<br /><br /><br />---<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>ORIGINAL REVIEW: August 2015</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>eXCuSE mE I CAn'T BrEAThE.</b> It's a book about books. ABOUT BOOKS!!!! It's about book smuggling, and book burning, and book controlling. It's <i>incredible</i>...although, to be honest, I <i>did</i> have a rather long list of quibbles about it. But I enjoyed it. I <i>really</i> enjoyed it. The characters were complex (AND DIVERSE OMG I AM SO HAPPY) and the story was exciting and bookish and bloody. The last 50-pages gave me <i>goosebumps</i> AND made me squawk a laugh out loud. Although that might've been a trauma laugh??? Probably??? STILL. <b>I love this book.</b><br /><br /><b>It's set in an Alternate Universe!</b> So not dystopian! It's more like a fantasy world, set in 2025, where owning your own books is illegal. The Alexandria Library never got destroyed and kinda controls everything. And I mean, <i>everything</i>. It's got a very 19th century vibe to it, so I figure that's when the printing press SHOULD have been invented, but since it wasn't (they killed the dude who invented it, okay?!) everyone is really rather stuck in that era. Books = progression. <br /><br /><b>I have to admit, though, the world-building confused me.</b> There's magic??? Maybe??? They can, like, send books/people/things with a kind of teleportation. And they have these "blank" books, that can be written in and wiped by the Weird Controlling Library People. SO IS THIS MAGIC, OR SCIENCE OR WHAT??? I was <i>so</i> confused. It actually soured the beginning of the book for me. <br /><br />Like, in particular, the book starts off with Jess, as a 10yo, smuggling a book across town. BY RUNNING. Doesn't running draw attention to you? I have no idea why he wasn't sneaking, but instead running and I have no idea why when he passed this line, or something, everyone stopped chasing him. THE BEGINNING OF THE BOOK MAKES 0% SENSE TO ME. <br /><br /><b>Buuuut...worldbuilding aside, I seriously loved it!</b> I really loved Jess! He was a pretty non-nonsense sort of guy, but he liked books. Like LOVED books. Like, he-will-risk-bodily-harm-to-protect-a-book. Omg. I love you Jess. His family are all book smugglers, too, but his dad wanted him to sign up for the tricky task of getting hired by the Alexandria Library so...basically he'd have an inside mole. <b>I love books about families!</b> I only wish this was MORE about the smuggling side, but I think that'll come in later books?! Jess also has a twin, Brenden, who seems like a regular adorable psychopath. Exciting! I hope he features more in the next books too.<br /><br />There's also a stack of other characters. Seriously, it's a BIG CAST. And they were all different and well developed and dynamic and interesting and AFJDSAKLFD I CANNOT LOVE THEM ALL ENOUGH. <br /><br /><i>(Jess meets most of these characters as his classmates when they're going through lessons to get into the library:)</i><br /><b>+Thomas:</b> He's German and huge and SUCH A SWEETIE! I loved Thomas. Although he was an inventor and, erm, the book starts off telling us they KILL inventors, so I was freaking out for Thomas so much. He was so naive and...genius.<br /><b>+ Khalila:</b> She was middle eastern and SUPER SMART. She's like the Hermoine. She scored 100%...like seriously?! The test was insanely hard. She had a softer side, but she was all tough and I-don't-need-your-help-I-am-not-a-damsel. I LOVE HER.<br /><b>+ Dario:</b> He's Spanish and he and Jess just have this unreasonable rivalry, which is hilarious.<br /><b>+ Glain:</b> She's Welsh, so she and Jess clashed on principle of their country's rivalry, and she didn't have as much interestingness as the others.<br /><b>+ Wolfe:</b> EXCUSE ME WHILE I SCREECH MY LOVE FOR WOLFE!! He's the super cranky instructor. You know the kind that nearly sets his classroom on fire in the first lesson. (Love 'im.) And he's MEAN and UNFAIR and such a really adorable softie inside...gah. He's like a coconut. And also I shipped him so hard with <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Santi. LIKE OMG. A surprisingly endearing LGBT romance, that was just <i>there</i> and accepted and <i>normal</i>?!??! YES PLEASE AND THANK YOU. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I really wish there was a whole BOOK about Wolfe. Like an entire series. LIKE I WOULD READ ALL THE THINGS ABOUT WOLFE. I adore meanie softies.<br /><br /><b>It's quite exciting also!</b> Lots of war (although I have no idea WHY there was a war...again...not sure if I'm just deluded and didn't <i>get</i> the world-building, or whether it was missing something) and bloodshed and pain and a bit of torture too. It wasn't super face paced though. Especially when they were learning and studying. But the writing was BEAUTIFUL and addictive. Although <b>it's NOT a book you can breeze through.</b> It took me 3 days to read, whereas a book usually takes ONE DAY for me. <br /><br /><b>I LOVED IT EVEN IF I HAVE QUIBBLES.</b> I adored the characters and I luuuuurve books about books. It's so creative and interesting. I just hope either a) the next book explains the world better, or b) I reread it at some point and GET it this time. And, erm, prepare to be choked with feels at the ending. PREPARE FOR A WICKED CLIFFHANGER. I love this book so much I may need to sob.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5008523978187659338" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1140722966" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1140722966" />
    <a title="Faye, la Patata" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7650833-faye-la-patata"><img alt="Faye, la Patata" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557835753p2/7650833.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1140722966?book_show_action=true">Dec 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Faye, la Patata" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Faye, la Patata" href="/user/show/7650833-faye-la-patata">Faye, la Patata</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=male-pov">male-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=humans-are-scary">humans-are-scary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=good-hero">good-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=haunting-narration">haunting-narration</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=refreshing">refreshing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=heartwrenching">heartwrenching</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=slow-and-steady-romance">slow-and-steady-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=fun-narration">fun-narration</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1140722966" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1491540509644519746"><blockquote>
  <em>Dear bookworms of the world,</em>
  <br/>
  <br/>
  <em>You need this book in your life. If you don't buy, read, and love this as much as I did, well, I ain't gonna be your friend no more.</em>
  <br/>
  <br/>
  <em>With much love, Faye.</em>
</blockquote><br/>Okay, I kid, I'll still be your friend nevertheless, but do you think I'm kidding about the awesomeness of this book? Let me tell you something: I don't always give books 5 stars. But when I do, there are two categories: 5 stars, and <strong>5-fucking-fantastic-stars.</strong><br/><br/>When you have a story with a<strong> <em>male her</em></strong></span>
  <span id="freeText1491540509644519746" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <em>Dear bookworms of the world,</em>
  <br>
  <br>
  <em>You need this book in your life. If you don't buy, read, and love this as much as I did, well, I ain't gonna be your friend no more.</em>
  <br>
  <br>
  <em>With much love, Faye.</em>
</blockquote><br>Okay, I kid, I'll still be your friend nevertheless, but do you think I'm kidding about the awesomeness of this book? Let me tell you something: I don't always give books 5 stars. But when I do, there are two categories: 5 stars, and <strong>5-fucking-fantastic-stars.</strong><br><br>When you have a story with a<strong> <em>male hero, who fricking loves books,</em></strong> in an alternate history fantasy setting who travels with a group of amazing friends and a sarcastic, strict, likeable mentor, and who eventually goes against a <em>
  <strong>LIBRARY CORPORATION</strong>
</em> that is keen on controlling how books are used and made, well, I'm sorry, but doesn't that just scream <strong>5-fucking-fantastic-stars</strong> to you?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1436886293ra/15514731.gif" alt="" width="500" height="209" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I really, really, really love this book. I read it with an open mind a month ago, not knowing of the premise or the author, and was absolutely blown away by how amazing and original and refreshing it was.<br><br>1.) <strong>It's about books.</strong> A book about books. That already sounds awesome, doesn't it?
  <strong> It's about a world torn by books</strong>
 - by people who want to control how books are made and shelved and copied and stored, and by people who'd rather burn <strong>(!!!!)</strong> and eat <strong>(?!?!?!)</strong> books than have their lives compromised by an oppressing system where having original copies of books can be the death of you. <strong>It's about a group of friends </strong>(or, okay, enemies-turned-forced-acquaintances-turned-friends)<strong>  who love books and seek to protect them in various ways, going so far as to put their lives on the line in order to make sure they're safe from harm.</strong><br><br>2.) <b>The library is the freaking villain. </b>Okay, maybe not the library itself, but the people behind it who are pulling the strings? Yup. They're so drunk with their power and how they control the books and the people with their system that they say "OFF WITH THEIR HEADS!" quicker than the Queen of Hearts on crack. And, guys?<strong> They're the ultimate book hoarders. They're us, except on steroids. </strong>And by steroids, I mean nasty, nasty steroids. You don't wanna mess with these guys, unless you're Jess Brightwell, of course.<br><br>3.)
  <strong> </strong>
<strong>Male hero who loves books as much as we do. </strong>Jess comes from a book smuggling family. They find original copies, and then sell them to collectors, and getting the books to these collectors is no easy feat as they have to evade the authorities and these automated stone lions that come to life when they sniff some black-market-mischief. And then one day, upon delivering a book to a collector, Jess witnessed a man eat the only copy of an ancient historian's book like it was nothing, and that was when he realized this book smuggling thing just wasn't his cup of tea.<br><br>I have nothing but love for this guy. <strong>You can really tell how much he cares for books a lot, and how much he's willing to go so, so far just for them.</strong> How far would we go for knowledge? How far would we go in order to make sure that knowledge is easily accessible? What would we do if we have to choose between books and the people who thirst for freedom? Plus, I just love his personality, and I love his interactions with his friends (who are all so very diverse, guys... heck, there's even an interracial romance among them, HOLY MOTHER OF EPICBALLS) and with his mentor who is a bundle of complexity because you love and hate him at the same time.<br><br>4.) 
  <strong>The writing and the world-building are amazing.</strong>
 The writing reminded me so much of Brandon Sanderson's - it's not purple-prose and verbose and uses more simple words than other fantasy/AU novels, and yet, they still say so much and connect you to the story easily and efficiently. The way they were weaved and connected felt so fricking lyrical and poetic and romantic despite the fact that the story contained themes of oppression, bleakness, and the need for freedom from an unfair system. <strong>The book was so entertaining and so heartbreaking and so heartwarming, all at the same time, that it left me in tears and in joy and at the edge of my seat.</strong><br><br>All in all, this book is the book of my dreams. Its place is right there beside Brandon Sanderson, and that's a big, big, BIG deal right there.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1491540509644519746" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1366225575" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1366225575" />
    <a title="Darth J " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18974711-darth-j"><img alt="Darth J " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456429148p2/18974711.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

Despite having an interesting premise that would appeal to most bibliophiles, I felt like there was nothing there to hook me immediately. There were animatronic lions and statues, and then steam powered carriages for some reason (this book is set in the near future so it was really odd). It felt like a smattering of other successful stories right now in the market had bits picked from them and this was what was trying to be cobbled out of it. Let's not even mention the "we have to keep books (read: education) from commoners" thing.<br><br>There's just no warmth or heart here to keep me interested.</span>

<div id="review_2282482741" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2282482741" />
    <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz"><img alt="Helena of Eretz ✰" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596076376p2/27036454.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2282482741?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helena of Eretz ✰" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz">Helena of Eretz ✰</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780451472397" href="/book/show/23398607-ink-and-bone">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=magical-libraries">magical-libraries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=hardback">hardback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=best-of-2015">best-of-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2282482741" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9846445812157213852">So, I’d just like to point out that I was a weird child growing up. I <b>adored</b> mythology more than any other type of bedtime story and I began reading both <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/516650.The_Iliad' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Iliad</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77201.The_Odyssey' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Odyssey</a> at age 10. I know, <i>weird</i>. Having said that, I was heartbroken when I later discovered that these were the only two Ancient Greek epics surviving, out of the eight that were written, now known as the Epic Cycle. The thought of destroyed books makes me despair in agony. Now I’m certain that I’m not the only person who st</span>
  <span id="freeText9846445812157213852" style="display:none">So, I’d just like to point out that I was a weird child growing up. I <b>adored</b> mythology more than any other type of bedtime story and I began reading both <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/516650.The_Iliad" rel="nofollow noopener">The Iliad</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77201.The_Odyssey" rel="nofollow noopener">The Odyssey</a> at age 10. I know, <i>weird</i>. Having said that, I was heartbroken when I later discovered that these were the only two Ancient Greek epics surviving, out of the eight that were written, now known as the Epic Cycle. The thought of destroyed books makes me despair in agony. Now I’m certain that I’m not the only person who still gets emotional over the destruction of the Library of Alexandria. ALL OF THOSE BOOKS…GONE!!! GONE FOREVER!!! NEVER TO BE SEEN OR READ EVER AGAIN! :(<br><br>Luckily, Ink &amp; Bone brings into question…what if the Library of Alexandria had never been destroyed?!<br><br>Well, according to Rachel Caine, had the Library of Alexandria survived, the world would be <b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13259220-fahrenheit-451" rel="nofollow noopener">Fahrenheit 451</a> on steroids</b>. Finally, I’ve come across a dystopian novel that I’ve genuinely enjoyed. This was sooo original and I loved every second of it!!! Thus, I am awarding this novel <b>4.5 stars</b>!!!<br><blockquote>
<br> <i>“They've all got stories, Jess thought. I need to know them. Best of all, he could know them. He could learn anything here. It felt like limitless possibilities.”</i><br>
</blockquote><br>I’m not going to lie, I considered putting this on hold (for a second time), whilst I struggled to get through the Prologue and Chapter One. But once Chapter Two began, the plot was so well-paced for the remainder of the novel that it completely made up for it!!! Despite this being a very short book (only 350-ish pages), it feels much longer, but it’s completely worth it!<br><br>First of all, I’d like to address everyone who compared this novel to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15710432-harry-potter-and-the-philosopher-s-stone" rel="nofollow noopener">Harry Potter</a>…Every book that requires training at a school does not need to be compared to Harry Potter. Don’t get me wrong, I love Harry Potter as much as the next person (In fact, it’s even #2 on my Favourite Books of All Time list), but: 1) J.K. Rowling did not patent books about schools, 2) Books about schools existed <i>long before</i> Harry Potter (cough <i>Enid Blyton</i> cough), and 3) Books about schools will exist <i>long after</i> Harry Potter. Comparisons to Harry Potter as marketing ploys really get on my nerves! If there were magic being taught at this school, I’d understand…but they’re being taught to be scholars and how the Library functions! There is absolutely no magic in this book (Well, there is alchemy – which isn't being taught – but no spells or potions!)!!! Ugh.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1531176204ra/25947978.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>PSA:</b> As this is a dystopian novel, it might interest you to know that there is also quite a bit of death in this novel, which I found to be quite unexpected. There are also a number of surprising twists and turns!<br><br>Ink &amp; Bone is centred around Jess, who comes from a family of smugglers. They smuggle books because the ownership of physical books is now illegal (and punishable by death because “when you steal a book, you steal from the world”) in the year 2025. Everyone is given blanks (which very much resembles eBooks on a tablet), or a codex (which is a more expensive version of blanks), and the books that are loaded onto there are strictly controlled. The world is run in a dictatorship-type manner by the Great Library, who control the world’s knowledge because as everyone knows: knowledge is power. The Library’s motto is actually <i>tota est scientia</i> (or <i>knowledge is all</i>). The Library would rather the world go up in flames around them than let any harm come to the books. People who work for the library would even die to protect the books from harm. They also use automaton lions, sphinxes, and soldiers which are awfully scary! <br><br>There are many who protest the Library’s control including the smugglers, who profit from selling valuable books to those who can afford it, and the Burners, who set fires to the books (and even themselves) in protest with Greek Fire. We also have the perverted ink-lickers who <b>eat</b> the books in order to completely possess its knowledge. <br><br>One of the best aspects of this novel, however, is its <i>diversity</i>. All of the characters are from around world, practice various religions, and have different sexual orientations! <b>Scholar Christopher Wolfe and High Garda Captain Niccolo Santi</b> are not only the children’s mentors, but also a wonderful gay couple. Wolfe was actually my favourite character!!! <b>Jess Brightwell and Morgan Hault</b> are both English and so bloody cute. <b>Glain Wathen</b> is Welsh, yet also the bad-arse muscle out of them all. <b>Thomas Schreiber</b> is a German inventor and a giant teddy bear! &lt;3 <b>Dario Santiago</b> is a pompous Spaniard LOL. And finally, <b>Khalila Seif</b> is a Saudi Arabian Muslim <i>genius</i>. And I absolutely love every single one of them (yes, even Dario haha)! All of these characters meet at the Great Library of Alexandria in Egypt in order to fight for their places within the Library’s workforce. Some will end up as Scholars (archivists), others will end up as part of the Garda (soldiers), and, in rare instances, others will end up as Obscurists (alchemists).<br><br>If you haven't tried this book yet, I highly recommend it. Amongst the plethora of YA dystopia, this is definitely a hidden gem. :D</span>
  <a data-text-id="9846445812157213852" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1137799999" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1137799999" />
    <a title="Alyssa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8472395-alyssa"><img alt="Alyssa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500935920p2/8472395.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1137799999?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyssa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyssa" href="/user/show/8472395-alyssa">Alyssa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780451472397" href="/book/show/23398607-ink-and-bone">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8472395-alyssa?shelf=2015-releases">2015-releases</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1137799999" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18192546567779446152"><strong>
  <a href='http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2015/07/interview-with-rachel-caine-author-of.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>GIVEAWAY: find out the title of the sequel to Ink and Bone - and win in a copy of <i>Ink and Bone</i>!</a>
</strong><br/><br/><br/>***<a href='http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2015/06/review-ink-and-bone-by-rachel-caine.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br/><br/>Ink and Bone by Rachel Caine<br/>Book One of The Great Library series<br/>Publisher: NAL<br/>Publication Date: July 7, 2015<br/>Rating: 4 stars<br/>Source: Review copy sent by the publisher<br/><br/>Summary (from Goodreads):<br/><br/>In an exhilarating new series, New York Times bestselling author Rachel Caine rewrites history, creating a dangerous world where the Great Library of Alexandria has </span>
  <span id="freeText18192546567779446152" style="display:none"><strong>
  <a href="http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2015/07/interview-with-rachel-caine-author-of.html" rel="nofollow noopener">GIVEAWAY: find out the title of the sequel to Ink and Bone - and win in a copy of <i>Ink and Bone</i>!</a>
</strong><br /><br /><br />***<a href="http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2015/06/review-ink-and-bone-by-rachel-caine.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br /><br />Ink and Bone by Rachel Caine<br />Book One of The Great Library series<br />Publisher: NAL<br />Publication Date: July 7, 2015<br />Rating: 4 stars<br />Source: Review copy sent by the publisher<br /><br />Summary (from Goodreads):<br /><br />In an exhilarating new series, New York Times bestselling author Rachel Caine rewrites history, creating a dangerous world where the Great Library of Alexandria has survived the test of time.…<br /><br />Ruthless and supremely powerful, the Great Library is now a presence in every major city, governing the flow of knowledge to the masses. Alchemy allows the Library to deliver the content of the greatest works of history instantly—but the personal ownership of books is expressly forbidden.<br /><br />Jess Brightwell believes in the value of the Library, but the majority of his knowledge comes from illegal books obtained by his family, who are involved in the thriving black market. Jess has been sent to be his family’s spy, but his loyalties are tested in the final months of his training to enter the Library’s service.<br /><br />When he inadvertently commits heresy by creating a device that could change the world, Jess discovers that those who control the Great Library believe that knowledge is more valuable than any human life—and soon both heretics and books will burn.…<br /><br />What I Liked:<br /><br />My first Rachel Caine read! Isn't it pretty?! Take a look at the spine, if you have a print copy (hardcover especially) - so gorgeous! It reminds of how the spines of old books used to be. Not flashy with the book's title printed across, but very much like an old bound book's spine! Excellent work there, NAL, with the book's spine and cover! And excellent work, Caine, for writing a very intriguing novel, which I enjoyed!<br /><br />Jess comes from a family of book smugglers, in a time in which it is illegal to own printed novels. Everything can be accessed from the Great Library in Alexandria, but owning books is against the law. Jess is sent by his father to the library to train with other students to get a position in the Great Librarian - but also to be a spy for his family, and get books his family to smuggle. But soon Jess realizes that much more is at stake than his family's business, and that the Great Library isn't what it seems. His loyalties will be tested in many ways, and Jess will be forced to choose a side.<br /><br />This book is so OMINOUS. Right from the start, I was slightly worried for Jess. The entire book has a suspenseful and dark tone - I was always wondering when Jess would get caught, or when the next person would die, etc. I was on the edge of my seat, trying to figure out what would happen next. This book moves a bit slow, but the mood is very dark and ominous. Someone was always being killed or worried about it. Scary! Not that the book is scary. But dealing with print books and hiding who you are (a print book smuggler) would make anyone uneasy (to say the least).<br /><br />This book is written in third person limited, to Jess. Jess is a very intelligent boy, who really appreciates print books. His father is very hard on him, and sends him on deliveries all the time, instead of his time brother Brendan. And then Jess's father pays to have him take the exams to receive education at the Great Library. With about twenty other students, Jess goes to Alexandria. Jess is quiet yet clever, nimble and street-smart. A jack-of-all-trades. I think I like him, though I struggled a bit to connect with him initially.<br /><br />The supporting characters are one of the best and most well-written part of this book. Jess is the protagonist, but there are several other students that play critical roles in this novel. There were twenty at first, but only six spots are open. Dario, Jess's roommate in Alexandria, is a handful, but I think I like him when he was first introduced (but he's a handful). Khalila is a poised and intelligent girl. Thomas is a friendly giant with a very creative engineering mind. Glain is a cold Welsh girl. Morgan is a late arrival, mysterious and odd. Wolfe is the Scholar who is in charge of the students, and he is ruthless and a bit scary. Captain Santi keeps guard of the students and Scholar. Wolfe might be my favorite character! He's an interesting one, once you get to know him. All of these characters are. You might start out disliking one or two, but will fall for all of them by the end!<br /><br />There IS romance in this book! And I love it because for about 80% of the book, the romance is pretty much not important. It doesn't really start arising until about 50% of the book, but even then, it's just there. It's not a plot-mover, it's not all-encompassing or consuming. It's sweet and I love watching Jess fall for the girl. It's a subtle romance, though you know it's coming when the characters meet. No love triangle! And to make things better, there are other pairs of characters involved in their own romances in the book as well. One made me particularly happy - one the train is when we/Jess makes the discovery (you'll know which I mean when you read the book) - I KNEW IT!<br /><br />Speaking of I KNEW IT! - there was something else in this book that I had my suspicions about from the beginning - AND I WAS RIGHT! I'm very paranoid and suspicious and as soon as I read about this one thing in the book, I was like, hmmm, but couldn't they be doing this with this... and I was right! Very vague, I know, but I'm feeling triumphant. Good instincts will catch it!<br /><br />The characterization is really good - Jess grows a great deal in this book. He has to choose sides and paths and decisions again and again, over and over, and he proves his intelligence and perceptiveness and maturity over and over. I personally thought he developed quite a bit as a character, and not just him. He reminded me a bit of Darrow from Pierce Brown's Red Rising.<br /><br />The world-building is amazing! Caine is a painter with words - the setting and imagery and descriptions are captivating and lovely. There are many different scenery/landscapes in this book, and Caine makes each one unique in its own way. The world-building is very well-written - Caine definitely did a good job of creating this world and story! Though I can't wait to dig deeper in the next book(s).<br /><br />The plot is slow. I will say that as a negative below - the story moves slowly. It's an interesting story, and I was anxious while reading (I see this as a good thing), but the plot is slow. There is plenty of scheming and deaths and betrayals and twists and true natures revealed and all kinds of shenanigans. The ending had me sad and angry and scared and wanting much, much more. In a positive way, if that makes sense.<br /><br />Overall, I very much enjoyed this book! I'm looking forward to the next volume in this series - I need it! So many things to be fixed!<br /><br />What I Did Not Like:<br /><br />Like I said above, this book's pacing is slow. It took me longer than usual to read this one, and obviously it's not due to the book's length (this book is short), or genre (it's a futuristic fantasy type, which I do love). The story is very interesting and I was never bored, but it's a slow-moving book, in my opinion. <br /><br />Would I Recommend It:<br /><br />Yes! I would! Fantasy fans, contemporary fans, basically anyone who likes books... try the book about books! This book was pretty impressive, and definitely got me thinking about books in general. I could not live without my print books! Anyway, this is a Young Adult book, but it is highly suitable for adults. It almost reads like an adult book! Younger teens could read this one, the content isn't too bad (the violence is the heaviest stuff, and it's not bad).<br /><br />Rating:<br /><br />4 stars. My first Rachel Caine book, a successful! I'm not sure I'll ever read her vampire series, but I know I'll be continuing with this one!</span>
  <a data-text-id="18192546567779446152" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1300745408" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1300745408" />
    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1300745408?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=2015-read">2015-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1300745408" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13108384754651665788"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436407809i/15453790._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>Reread 04/18</u>
</b> : Skimming through this again because I just got the arc of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25890355.Paper_and_Fire__The_Great_Library___2_' title='Paper and Fire (The Great Library, #2) by Rachel Caine' rel='nofollow noopener'>Paper and Fire</a>. WOOT!<br/><br/><b><u>Actual rating</u> : <s>3.5</s> Happily rounded up at 4 because DUH. <i>BOOKS.</i></b><br/><br/>In my honest opinion <b>the strength of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20643052.Ink_and_Bone__The_Great_Library___1_' title='Ink and Bone (The Great Library, #1) by Rachel Caine' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ink and Bone</a> lies first in the plot, which is entertaining as hell, and in the world-building, which contains several of my main interests</b> : think books, automatons, alchemy, a dystopian world ruled by Librarians who control every knowledge (or aim to) and an academy blended together. Exciting? FUCK Y</span>
  <span id="freeText13108384754651665788" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436407809i/15453790._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>Reread 04/18</u>
</b> : Skimming through this again because I just got the arc of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25890355.Paper_and_Fire__The_Great_Library___2_" title="Paper and Fire (The Great Library, #2) by Rachel Caine" rel="nofollow noopener">Paper and Fire</a>. WOOT!<br><br><b><u>Actual rating</u> : <s>3.5</s> Happily rounded up at 4 because DUH. <i>BOOKS.</i></b><br><br>In my honest opinion <b>the strength of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20643052.Ink_and_Bone__The_Great_Library___1_" title="Ink and Bone (The Great Library, #1) by Rachel Caine" rel="nofollow noopener">Ink and Bone</a> lies first in the plot, which is entertaining as hell, and in the world-building, which contains several of my main interests</b> : think books, automatons, alchemy, a dystopian world ruled by Librarians who control every knowledge (or aim to) and an academy blended together. Exciting? FUCK YEAH.<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436407810i/15453791._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>► <b>Random facts you might want to know about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20643052.Ink_and_Bone__The_Great_Library___1_" title="Ink and Bone (The Great Library, #1) by Rachel Caine" rel="nofollow noopener">Ink and Bone</a></b> (because there's no way I'm spoiling the story for you)<br><br>✔ After reading I went to my bookshelves and HUGGED my paperbacks. Not my Kindle. The thing kind of scared me. <br><br>✔ It presents <b>an alternative history that actually MAKES SENSE</b> (most of the time) : think about our history with a twist, the uprising of the Great Library, an organization that controls every book and then, holds a great deal of power. No <i>press</i>. No Gutenberg. I know, *GASP*<br><br>✔ Oh, they have lions automatons as guards : HOW AWESOME IS THAT???<br><br>✔ I loved the concept of <b>Codex</b> and every invention and gadget, really. I don't want to give away too much, but let's say that the Great Library developed a number of mechanisms, first of all the ability to transfer and erase words on every book sold, because they're all <i>blanks</i>, sort of ereaders controlled by the Library while originals are carefully kept in Alexandria. <i>An example?</i> Look at your book, and imagine that it would be possible for someone else to alter or erase its content in one second without even being at the same place as you. OMG BUT THAT'S POSSIBLE! Frightening, right? I thought so. Especially given that printed books are outlawed. <br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436407810i/15453792._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Concerning the <b>characterization</b>, I have to admit that I'm not completely convinced by it because <b>it lacks of depth</b>. Indeed the characters felt quite <i>blank</i> sometimes - not in a boring way, but <b>they weren't fleshed-out enough in my opinion</b>, especially the secondary ones like Jess's fellow students, who were border stereotypical on some aspects. That's why I'd have wanted them to be less transparent in their intentions and more <i>intricate</i>. However, I did enjoy Wolfe's character a lot, because he was complex and multi-layered : here's the kind of characters I can love. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"I suppose you want me to apologize for calling you a bastard."<br>"No need," Santi said. "You should hear what his <i>friends</i> call him."<br>" I have friends?" Wolfe said.<br>"They don't care to admit it in public."</b>
</blockquote><br>As for <b>Jess</b>, the main character, I'm afraid that my complaints prove to be the same. Indeed although I can't say that I didn't <i>care</i> about him because it would be false, at the same time I can't deny that <b>I kept feeling that something was missing to completely win me</b>. <i>Oh, well</i>. I don't know. Perhaps I'm not used to that kind of books (which emphasizes on the plot, let's say) anymore. Indeed almost every one of my favorite authors (Marchetta, Moskowitz, Robin Hobb, even) focus primarily on the characterization and that's okay with me, because that's what I seek most of the time. Not here : not that Jess's character wasn't interesting, but he never stood out either. Now, perhaps does it serve the story's purpose, in a way? Concerning his personality, <b>he's not flawless and I'm glad he isn't</b> : indeed he makes mistakes, he has at first a restrained vision of the world (yes, he's sometimes full of <s>shit</s> stereotypes, but now, he's 16, give him a break) but how in the world could it be different, tell me? From his upbringing spent as a smuggler for his family's business to his training in the Academy, he has always been <i>used</i>, and <b>genuinely doesn't know how to deal with real relationships</b>. However something about him rubbed me the wrong way, and that's the fact that he cares about books more than people. Well, even as a book lover (no shit) it made me a little uncomfortable at times, I must confess. Fortunately it doesn't stay that way, because despite the fact that books are rare in his world, I wouldn't have stand a character who happily watches people getting starved and killed because of books. Sorry guys. I'm TEAM HUMANS. (I'm French, after all. Yes, that's relevant. You'll see)<br><br><b>But then, little by little, he <i>evolves</i></b>. Day after day, he realizes that the world is not near as simple as he thought he was. Page after page, we get to know him better, to <i>understand</i> him more. Chapter after chapter, the choices he has to face become more and more difficult and the lines between right or wrong blur... For that, I thank you, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/15292.Rachel_Caine" title="Rachel Caine" rel="nofollow noopener">Rachel Caine</a>. For that, <b>I'm eager to read the next book because I feel how strong his potential can be</b>.<br><br>Finally, for most of the book, I got the feeling that the <b>romance was... Well... I'd say "low-cute"</b>. <i>What is it, you're asking?</i> It means that I'm happy for them, kind of, but I don't care and to me it was unnecessary since the author openly didn't focus on it, so much that the story would have been as great without it. Now, (don't hit me) but that's what I thought about the romance in <i>Harry Potter</i> too. I just don't care. That's not why I loved the books. So, yeah, I wasn't a big fan of this romance which stayed in no-chemistry territory, until, until, <b>until suddenly I started to <i>feel</i> something, and that was as glorious as unexpected</b>.<br><br>By the way, I realized that I forgot to talk about this so... <b>There is another romance in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20643052.Ink_and_Bone__The_Great_Library___1_" title="Ink and Bone (The Great Library, #1) by Rachel Caine" rel="nofollow noopener">Ink and Bone</a>, and I ship them SO hard.</b><br><br>Now, and that's something I rarely write, but to me <b>the pacing was perfection</b> : I was never EVER bored and the writing just flowed smoothly, making the read <b>completely addictive</b>, and some parts were so full of tension that my heartbeat increased.<br><br>PS : French are rebels, eat lambs and drink red wine : of course they do &gt;.&lt; <br>PS2 : No, Dario, Spanish wine isn't better than Cahors. DUH.<br>PS3 : I might be (a little) subjective. MAY-BE.<br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote><br><br></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7998483843244974082">In this alternate history type of fantasy, the Library of Alexandria was never destroyed, which ended up affecting the world profoundly. But - surprisingly - not necessarily in ways that are good. The world has developed in a very different direction, scientifically and politically, and the Library keeps a stranglehold over the ownership of books, forbidding private ownership of hard copies on pain of death (ereaders are fine, but the Library monitors the content) and ruthlessly destroying the p</span>
  <span id="freeText7998483843244974082" style="display:none">In this alternate history type of fantasy, the Library of Alexandria was never destroyed, which ended up affecting the world profoundly. But - surprisingly - not necessarily in ways that are good. The world has developed in a very different direction, scientifically and politically, and the Library keeps a stranglehold over the ownership of books, forbidding private ownership of hard copies on pain of death (ereaders are fine, but the Library monitors the content) and ruthlessly destroying the printing press each time it is invented. It's basically Amazon, in control and run amok. <br /><br />This is an intriguing and somewhat dark fantasy. Full review to come.</span>
