  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1115387274" />
    <a title="Nina (Every Word A Doorway)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32524334-nina-every-word-a-doorway"><img alt="Nina (Every Word A Doorway)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456070558p2/32524334.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1115387274?book_show_action=true">Nov 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nina (Every Word A Doorway)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nina (Every Word A Doorway)" href="/user/show/32524334-nina-every-word-a-doorway">Nina (Every Word A Doorway)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25814724-ink-and-bone">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32524334-nina-every-word-a-doorway?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1115387274" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14756054522511172088">Truth be told: <b>I liked the idea of this book more than I actually liked the book.</b><br/><br/>This was one of my most anticipated releases of 2015 and, well, it fell a bit flat. <br/><br/>Welcome to a world set in <b>2025</b> in which the <b>Great Library of Alexandria had never been burnt and destroyed</b>, and where books are a treasure hoarded and guarded by a powerful minority. Where the <b>private possession of books is illegal</b> and punishable (yes, I think we can agree that we’d all be screwed).<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>There are three parts to learnin</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText14756054522511172088" style="display:none">Truth be told: <b>I liked the idea of this book more than I actually liked the book.</b><br /><br />This was one of my most anticipated releases of 2015 and, well, it fell a bit flat. <br /><br />Welcome to a world set in <b>2025</b> in which the <b>Great Library of Alexandria had never been burnt and destroyed</b>, and where books are a treasure hoarded and guarded by a powerful minority. Where the <b>private possession of books is illegal</b> and punishable (yes, I think we can agree that we’d all be screwed).<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>There are three parts to learning: information, knowledge, and wisdom. A mere accumulation of information is not knowledge, and a treasure of knowledge is not in itself, wisdom. <br />The Library holds itself to be the keeper of both knowledge and wisdom, but it is not true. So much should never be held in the hands of so few, for it is a natural, venal habit of men to hold power. And knowledge is the purest form of power.</i>
</blockquote><br />16-yr old <b>Jess Brightwell</b> earns his keep in London as a Runner, a <b>book smuggler</b>. His father, however, realises that Jess would rather read the books than smuggle them (which he secretly does in his hideouts), and sends Jess to take the entry test for an <b>apprenticeship in the Great Library</b> of Alexandria – with a hidden agenda, that is. <br /><br />In this alternative future, librarians are at the top of the food chain, so to speak. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>”The first purpose of a librarian is to preserve and defend books.”<br /><br />“The books come first, Sir. Isn’t that how it should be? Books before men?”<br />Wolfe almost smiled. “As you see. They’re not children. They’re librarians.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><u>The Good</u><br />✓ The premise had captured my interest immediately because of the <b>unique concept</b>. <br />✓ The <b>main character was very likeable</b>, never running blindly into situations or hating on other people or any other pet peeves I sometimes experience with protagonists. However, he was <b>bland and not especially memorable</b>, and this extends to all the characters. Figures I’d list this under the things I liked and then I turn it into something I didn’t like. <br />✓ Romance barely existed in the first half, which was fine by me. <b>The romance that did occur was light</b> and neatly folded on the back seat as it should be. <br />✓ The plot ran at an unexciting average pace but, thank God, finally <b>accelerated in the last third of the book</b>. It was only at that point where my eyes became glued to the pages. <br />✓ The central <b>topics like loyalty, power, greed,</b> etc. were really intriguing! Even lgbtq and cultural diversity gets a short moment in the spotlight.<br /><br /><br /><u>The Bad</u><br />✗ <b>It’s 2025 but it reads like a novel set in the 18th century</b>. Advanced technology is hinted at, for example newspapers that automatically change (which has more to do with magic than technology seeing as it is still made out of paper but ok, let’s just… go with it), but the descriptions… I kept picturing medieval castles or ancient Egyptian architecture. London and Alexandria are modern cities, and Caine did not get this feeling across. Not one bit. Also, they travel large distances by train instead of taking the plane, but ok, it’s not like I want to badmouth ecological travelling in 2025.<br />✗ I thought the additional <b>element of magic was unnecessary and at times confusing</b>. The setting had already been special without the magic aspect, which was, by the way, barely explained. <br />✗ This is something minor but it bugged me: The way Jess had to help out with the family business made it seem as though the Brightwell’s weren’t doing well financially. Also, <b>Jess is teased for being a “lowborn”</b>, and yet at some stage <b>Caine notes that they are “a rich family”</b>. Sooo, kids get bullied because they're wealthy in 2025? Did I miss something?<br />✗ <b>It took Rachel Caine 240 pages to impress me</b>.<br /><br /><br />It’s not that I dislike <i>Ink and Bone</i> (Can I just point out that there are way too many YA books with Bone in their title? <i>Shadow and Bone</i>, <i>Daughter of Smoke and Bone</i>, … ). <b>The book wasn’t bad, it was fine</b>. But that’s the problem: It was just fine when I needed it to perform due to its amazing premise. <b>Throughout the book, I felt utterly unaffected by the characters and the plot.</b> The aspect I cared most for was hands down the books. I’m happy others enjoyed this but I need to be moved to give a book more than 3 stars. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14756054522511172088" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1595374772" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1595374772" />
    <a title="Carrie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36817401-carrie"><img alt="Carrie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415677371p2/36817401.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1595374772?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carrie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carrie" href="/user/show/36817401-carrie">Carrie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36817401-carrie?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1595374772" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13225773877240439563">The Great Library is in every city and controls the books of the world. Using alchemy to distribute the books those working for the library track down anyone with any in their possession and confiscate the materials. Ownership of books is expressly forbidden and anyone violating this law could even be sentenced to death. <br/><br/>Jess Brightwell's family has been involved in the black market for books. He's been raised to be a runner, delivering the books to those willing to pay the price and risk owners</span>
  <span id="freeText13225773877240439563" style="display:none">The Great Library is in every city and controls the books of the world. Using alchemy to distribute the books those working for the library track down anyone with any in their possession and confiscate the materials. Ownership of books is expressly forbidden and anyone violating this law could even be sentenced to death. <br /><br />Jess Brightwell's family has been involved in the black market for books. He's been raised to be a runner, delivering the books to those willing to pay the price and risk ownership. Jess has been sent to the library by his father to become a spy from the inside. He gets involved in the training only to find himself mixed up in the secrets of the library. <br /><br />Ink and Bone was one of those reads I enjoyed from start to finish. Such an interesting world Rachel Caine had created for anyone who loves to read. It's hard to imagine a world in which you could even die for trying to own a book but with bringing magic also into this world it became that much more interesting with the pursuit of keeping the books in the library's possession. <br /><br />The world building and character development in the story was excellent. A read that keeps you guessing in who you should be rooting for and who is actually the good guys versus the bad guys from start to finish. There are questions of who to trust and who is on the right side all throughout. A wonderful collection of characters that was just as fun getting to know as the plot behind the story. <br /><br />Overall, definitely a series that I would recommend. <br /><br />I received a copy from the publisher via NetGalley in exchange for an honest review.<br /><br />For more reviews please visit <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://carriesbookreviews.wordpress.com/">https://carriesbookreviews.wordpress....</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13225773877240439563" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1300060537" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1300060537" />
    <a title="Vanessa J." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19590155-vanessa-j"><img alt="Vanessa J." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468102148p2/19590155.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1300060537?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vanessa J." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vanessa J." href="/user/show/19590155-vanessa-j">Vanessa J.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=amazing-characters">amazing-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=alternate-history">alternate-history</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1300060537" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7101261709771270498"><b>4.5 out of 5 stars</b><br/><br/>Books, books, books, books, books, books, books, books, books, books.<br/><br/>Have I caught your attention already? No? Then, BOOOOOOOKSSS!!!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438193982ra/15676361.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The world of Ink and Bone is a world in which the Great Library of Alexandria still exists. They love books as much as you and me... but they take their love to a higher level: Books are precious and really valuable objects and they must all be preserved in the Great Library. Rare copies cannot be found anywhere and just the more privileged can own</span>
  <span id="freeText7101261709771270498" style="display:none"><b>4.5 out of 5 stars</b><br><br>Books, books, books, books, books, books, books, books, books, books.<br><br>Have I caught your attention already? No? Then, BOOOOOOOKSSS!!!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438193982ra/15676361.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The world of Ink and Bone is a world in which the Great Library of Alexandria still exists. They love books as much as you and me... but they take their love to a higher level: Books are precious and really valuable objects and they must all be preserved in the Great Library. Rare copies cannot be found anywhere and just the more privileged can own a single book. Plus, in this world, people eat and burn books as political protests.<br><br>Our protagonist Jess comes from a family of smugglers. He loves books, but he made a living by stealing them and selling them to other people. When he's old enough, his father sends him as an spy to the Great Library. There he starts learning things and realising some things that may or may not be lies and his trust starts to get smaller with time.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438193982ra/15676362.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Let's start saying how great the characters of this book were. They're from all parts of the world. There are people from France, Spain, the US, Egypt, Arabia, England, etc. There are the intelligent ones, the cunning ones, the lazy, the mysterious... really, there are all kinds of people here, and they're all intriguing in their own way.<br><br>My favourite character was by far the Scholar Wolfe. He's the one who teaches most of the lessons and runs the trials... and he's a complex one. At first, I had mixed feelings about him, but the more I read, the more I realised he was in fact great. He has many layers and sometimes it's impossible to decipher him, but I think that only made me love this more.<br><br>The other characters were amazing as well. Khalila, Thomas, Dario... they're all complex and flawed and they all have their own personalities.<br><br>Lately I've been complaining about the world building in books. Well, let me tell you one thing: This one had one of the best and most original world buildings I've read in books this year. We get to understand how the Burners think, how the Great Library works, we learn about the different jobs one can do in there... and yet there are still some mysteries, which in my opinion made the story more interesting.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1415239883ra/11755456.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I hadn't read anything by Rachel Caine until now, but if her writing in her other books are like the one in Ink and Bone, I am not going to doubt as to whether pick another one soon (probably Prince of Shadows).<br><br>The writing was all showing and not telling and I feaking loved it. The descriptions of Alexandria were beautiful. I could get a vivid picture of the Great Library and I got jealous of the characters, who were in the amazing world the author created.<br><br>When reading this book, I could not stop thinking about Harry Potter, but don't get me wrong - the concept of this was highly original. It reminded me of HP because if you change Hogwarts for The Great Library and the magic for alchemy and books, you get something similar to Ink and Bone. I must confess something, though: I prefer alchemy to magic by far. It's more intriguing in my opinion, and well, maybe I'm biased but alchemy was the beginning of chemistry and... I'll leave it there. I am starting to sound obsessive about chemistry.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438193982ra/15676363.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If you're looking for a creative alternate history world with a diverse cast of characters, beautiful writing and you love characters who love books, then Ink and Bone is just for you. I highly recommend it. Now, where is the sequel? I'm going to die waiting for it.<br><br>...<br><br><b>Pre-review:</b><br><br>Let's just take a moment of silence because I have read a book and I didn't hate it.<br><br>*a minute or two pass*<br><br>Thanks. Now, HELL YES, AT LAST!<br><br>Review to come. (Tomorrow, probably - it's past midnight here, I'm tired and it usually takes me an hour writing a review, especially if I have lots to say... I just hope I don't forget anything.)<br><br>P.S.: I want to be an Obscurist. Yeah, I know, they have their cons, but god, they're the best!<br><br>P.P.S.: As much as I love books, I would hate living in this world.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7101261709771270498" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1453874766" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1453874766" />
    <a title="Dannii Elle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle"><img alt="Dannii Elle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508499419p2/44487975.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1453874766?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dannii Elle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dannii Elle" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle">Dannii Elle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780749017224" href="/book/show/25090918-ink-and-bone">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=fantastic-fabrications">fantastic-fabrications</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1453874766" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5960462621378153543"><b>First Read: June 2017, Rating: 4/5 stars<br/>Second Read: April 2020, Rating: 4/5 stars</b><br/><br/>I was never not going to love a book with Library in the series name!<br/><br/>This is set in a world where the Library rules in place of a government. By keeping the knowledge contained in books closely guarded, and only available for scholars and those deemed worthy, it can both impede and advance societal growth as it sees fit. Technology is stunted, business advancements are thwarted and the Library maintains a tight lea</span>
  <span id="freeText5960462621378153543" style="display:none"><b>First Read: June 2017, Rating: 4/5 stars<br />Second Read: April 2020, Rating: 4/5 stars</b><br /><br />I was never not going to love a book with Library in the series name!<br /><br />This is set in a world where the Library rules in place of a government. By keeping the knowledge contained in books closely guarded, and only available for scholars and those deemed worthy, it can both impede and advance societal growth as it sees fit. Technology is stunted, business advancements are thwarted and the Library maintains a tight leash on its citizens. The all seeing and all powerful Library seems like an unbreakable patriarchal structure, but that might just be what they want you to think.<br /><br />I adored this unique world and found its politics surrounding the spreading of information and knowledge to provide intriguing points for discussion and thought, within the book. It did take a little while for me to acquaint myself with the particulars of the political structure, but once I had done so I was mesmerised with the layers to this fascinating governing regime.<br /><br />This is not my first time reading Caine's writing and I have been previously unimpressed. I am so glad I decided to give her another go as the authentic characters, the thrilling plot, and most especially this extraordinary world all combined to both restore my faith in this author and provide a leading example of YA dystopia done right!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5960462621378153543" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2049895098" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2049895098" />
    <a title="Melindam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36434323-melindam"><img alt="Melindam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484595601p2/36434323.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2049895098?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melindam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melindam" href="/user/show/36434323-melindam">Melindam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/43291854-ink-and-bone">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36434323-melindam?shelf=books-and-or-libraries">books-and-or-libraries</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2049895098" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1687813493485961054">BOOKS. LIBRARIES. ALCHEMISTS. SCHOOL. RIVALRY. ENMITY. FRIENDSHIP. BETRAYAL. DIVERSITY. SURVIVAL. <br/><br/>WOW. Just WOW. <br/><br/>This book had me at "Hello" / page 1. Honestly speaking, I don't know whether the effect would have been the same had I just read it instead of listening to the audiobook, but the narrator, Ben Allen was simply superb in making all the different characters come to life and the story to rock and roll. <br/><br/>As for the story in general, I think it was very well-written. It was tight-paced, te</span>
  <span id="freeText1687813493485961054" style="display:none">BOOKS. LIBRARIES. ALCHEMISTS. SCHOOL. RIVALRY. ENMITY. FRIENDSHIP. BETRAYAL. DIVERSITY. SURVIVAL. <br /><br />WOW. Just WOW. <br /><br />This book had me at "Hello" / page 1. Honestly speaking, I don't know whether the effect would have been the same had I just read it instead of listening to the audiobook, but the narrator, Ben Allen was simply superb in making all the different characters come to life and the story to rock and roll. <br /><br />As for the story in general, I think it was very well-written. It was tight-paced, tense, grim, inventive and exciting from beginning to end with some powerful, intriguing characters (Christopher Wolfe, Nicolo Santi, the horrible Artifex Magnus). <br />The world-building was jaw-dropping, the characters likeable, the romance convincing, but understated. It all came together in an amazingly strong start to a new series. I have fallen hook, line and sinker for it.<br /><br />There are undeniably some dystopian Harry Potter and Fahrenheit vibes, but it's a good, adolescent version of them at that. <br /><br />This story is not just about any library. THIS IS ABOUT THE GREAT LIBRARY.</span>

<div id="review_1273001249" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1273001249" />
    <a title="Mogsy (MMOGC)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4379514-mogsy-mmogc"><img alt="Mogsy (MMOGC)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1286325553p2/4379514.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1273001249?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mogsy (MMOGC)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mogsy (MMOGC)" href="/user/show/4379514-mogsy-mmogc">Mogsy (MMOGC)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=review-copy">review-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=alternate-history">alternate-history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=books-about-books">books-about-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1273001249" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14943322446614071954">5 of 5 stars at The BiblioSanctum <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://bibliosanctum.com/2015/07/10/book-review-ink-and-bone-by-rachel-caine/'>http://bibliosanctum.com/2015/07/10/b...</a><br/><br/>I spent most of the last week bouncing up and down telling everyone I know about Ink and Bone. In case I haven’t already gotten the chance to corner you with my mad ravings about this book, let me just tell you right now: this is an outstanding novel. Needless to say, it is going straight on my Favorites shelf and on my list of best books of 2015. There’s still almost half a year to go but I already know it’ll be hard one </span>
  <span id="freeText14943322446614071954" style="display:none">5 of 5 stars at The BiblioSanctum <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://bibliosanctum.com/2015/07/10/book-review-ink-and-bone-by-rachel-caine/">http://bibliosanctum.com/2015/07/10/b...</a><br /><br />I spent most of the last week bouncing up and down telling everyone I know about Ink and Bone. In case I haven’t already gotten the chance to corner you with my mad ravings about this book, let me just tell you right now: this is an outstanding novel. Needless to say, it is going straight on my Favorites shelf and on my list of best books of 2015. There’s still almost half a year to go but I already know it’ll be hard one to beat. Books of this caliber don’t come along often.<br /><br />Ink and Bone tells a tale of alternate history. As we all know, the invention of the printing press had an enormous impact on humanity, revolutionizing the way information is acquired, processed, and spread. But what if that never happened? Imagine a world where Johannes Gutenberg’s creation never came to light, a world where great minds like him were systematically silenced every time a new proposal for a method of printing came close to being realized. Imagine no ink plates, no moveable type, no presses – all innovations that were deemed too dangerous by an all-powerful ruling class that seeks to gather and control all knowledge, deciding who should have access to it, how and when.<br /><br />Jess Brightwell lives in such a world, where the only books that exist are original works or copies painstakingly written out by hand. By law they are all property of the Great Library of Alexandria, that powerful bastion of knowledge that never succumbed to destruction in this reality. The scholars of the Library strictly govern the distribution of books to the public, using a complex alchemical process to deliver content instantly to an individual’s personal Codex or blanks. As a result, traditionally bound books have become very popular on the black market, as has the illegal trade of smuggling them into the hands of private collectors and other rare book hunters. It’s risky, but the Brightwells have prospered in this business, and Jess’ father has decided to take it to the next level by sending his son into the Library’s service, hoping that having an inside man will benefit the family in the long run.<br /><br />But being a Library servant is a position of prestige, and as such, the trials used to seek out the best of the best are rigorous, brutal, and not always fair. I’ve always been fond of stories about magic schools, but Rachel Caine took the basis of that idea and made it all her own. Together with about two dozen other hopeful postulants, Jess Brightwell travels to the bright, magnificent city of Alexandria, home of the Great Library. Because knowledge is deemed paramount, training doesn’t just involve learning how to run one of the many daughter libraries present in every major city of the world; postulants are also taught to guard and protect it, keeping original works out of the public’s hands even if it means dying for the cause.<br /><br />As an avid reader, I of course find it difficult argue with the importance of knowledge. But to place its value above human lives? This should clue you into the kind of place our protagonist has landed in, and even with his book smuggling background, Jess is unprepared to learn about the corruption at the heart of Alexandria, or just how deep it lies.<br /><br />Despite its secrets (or perhaps because of them), the dark underside of the Great Library was a wonder to explore. Imagine a world where the personal ownership of books is forbidden – what a horrifying thought. But the story also appealed to a part of me that understood all too well why some people would resist the rule of the Library, or risk their lives to own a genuine paper book for the chance to hold a hefty volume in their hands, take in the heady scent of age and ink, as well as feel the hard leather of the binding or the crispness of the pages. Ink and Bone had that addictive and intoxicating effect on the delighted bookaholic in me, and I just couldn’t get enough.<br /><br />The novel is also so much more than that. I’ve never understood what a book hangover felt like until now, wishing I’m still in Jess Brightwell’s world. What Rachel Caine has created here is a rich and vibrant tableau, filled with beauty and amazing wonders but also no shortage of pain and darkness. Scenes of clean and shining Alexandria are juxtaposed by the ugliness of war in England as well as the destructive Greek Fire of the rebel Burners. The same alchemical processes that bring knowledge to the masses are also used to oppress them, keeping a watchful eye out for sedition or powering the nightmarish automatons that guard the Library from its enemies. All told, the world building is phenomenal but so is character development. Jess and his fellow postulants are part of an unforgettable cast, every one of them endearing themselves to me with their unique and individual personalities. Rare is it also to find an adult character in a YA novel as complex as Scholar Christopher Wolfe, who was not at all what I expected, and he quickly became a favorite.<br /><br />Once I started reading this book, I just couldn’t stop. It has raised the bar for the YA I’ll read for the rest of the year. But it doesn’t matter whether you’re a teen or an adult. Ink and Bone is for everyone, and a must-read for all who treasure the gift of the written word. A perfect mix of breathtaking fantasy and edge-of-your-seat dystopian fiction, this is a masterfully written novel guaranteed to hook you in.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14943322446614071954" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1273001249">

<div id="review_1133326022" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1133326022" />
    <a title="Ashley Marie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29787548-ashley-marie"><img alt="Ashley Marie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471208025p2/29787548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1133326022?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley Marie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley Marie " href="/user/show/29787548-ashley-marie">Ashley Marie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780451473134" href="/book/show/27068793-ink-and-bone">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29787548-ashley-marie?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29787548-ashley-marie?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29787548-ashley-marie?shelf=kickass-ladies">kickass-ladies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29787548-ashley-marie?shelf=i-own-it">i-own-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29787548-ashley-marie?shelf=fantasy-urban">fantasy-urban</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29787548-ashley-marie?shelf=fave-series">fave-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1133326022" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1191427934154169089">*If any of my writer friends love this series, hit me up!*<br/><br/>The original review was wrong. This deserves five stars and more. The whole series is so tightly plotted, and it all starts here. Khalila, Jess, Glain, Dario, Morgan, and my sweet Thomas. It's nuts to think the first time I read this was five years ago, because this series really feels timeless. Rachel Caine has a gift for tossing you off a cliff with five pages to go, doesn't matter which book in a series it is.<br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Four stars </span></span>
  <span id="freeText1191427934154169089" style="display:none">*If any of my writer friends love this series, hit me up!*<br /><br />The original review was wrong. This deserves five stars and more. The whole series is so tightly plotted, and it all starts here. Khalila, Jess, Glain, Dario, Morgan, and my sweet Thomas. It's nuts to think the first time I read this was five years ago, because this series really feels timeless. Rachel Caine has a gift for tossing you off a cliff with five pages to go, doesn't matter which book in a series it is.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Four stars doesn't feel like enough, but five almost feels like too much, even though I LOVED this.... ehhhh... dilemmas. 4 is good for now.<br /><br />I've never read the Morganville Vampires or any of Rachel Caine's other books (under other pseudonyms and what have you), but this was a great adventure. The cast was wonderfully diverse (and plausibly so-- none of them felt like "token" characters) and some compartment of my brain is already trying to fancast it, I'm positive. I'll probably wake up tomorrow and update this in a frenzy. <br /><br />A lot of critics are calling this a mix of Harry Potter and the Book Thief. And I can see it, I really can. The students-coming-to-school-from-elsewhere thing + the books. Oh the books. Mix in a little 1984 too (god yes) because the Library is possibly the scariest entity since Big Brother. Holy crap. THEY SEE EVERYTHING. <br /><br />So many of us bookworms like to fantasize about what the world might be like if the Library of Alexandria had never been destroyed. No Dark Ages, for one thing. But lemme tell you, this is one alternate history I would NOT like to live in. Instead of moving ahead with Gutenberg's printing press in the 1500s and making the written word available to everyone the world over, the Library has stomped out all similar inventions and relies on its Codex system when people want to read books. Original hand-inked copies are extremely valuable (duh) but once they get sucked into the Library's archives, that's it. Gone forever, never to see the light of day again. The whole Codex thing feels like... well, like a library. You don't have the actual book in your hands. Jess' family are book smugglers who do their best to keep original copies from being snatched away by the Library's guards, and it's very much life-or-death stuff. <br /><br />This whole concept makes me so unbelievably glad for the shelves of books I have upstairs, you don't even know. So glad for free speech and the fact that books are so accessible, because we could be living in a world like this one instead. <br /><br />Needless to say, I want a copy of this SO BAD. I also want the sequel JUST AS BAD. Dammit.<br /><br />update: This feels like such a crap review because I can't do this book justice. I may come back later and detail the characters. Maybe. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<div id="review_1257344749" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1257344749" />
    <a title="seak" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1805180-seak"><img alt="seak" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1410456529p2/1805180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1257344749?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="seak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="seak" href="/user/show/1805180-seak">seak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=arc-review">arc-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1257344749" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17380499944433322909">Knowledge is power and that's what the Library has been cultivating for centuries. Instead of releasing this knowledge to the world, it hoards it and if knowledge equals power, then the Library has proven that equation time and again. With an iron hold on the world and it's knowledge, it makes itself out to be the protector of information. Owning books is illegal. <br/><br/>But what it really presents is the stagnation of technology. And Jess is a book smuggler.<br/><br/>Original works are worth their weight in gol</span>
  <span id="freeText17380499944433322909" style="display:none">Knowledge is power and that's what the Library has been cultivating for centuries. Instead of releasing this knowledge to the world, it hoards it and if knowledge equals power, then the Library has proven that equation time and again. With an iron hold on the world and it's knowledge, it makes itself out to be the protector of information. Owning books is illegal. <br /><br />But what it really presents is the stagnation of technology. And Jess is a book smuggler.<br /><br />Original works are worth their weight in gold and Jess' family has been running books to every sort, but mostly those who will pay the hefty fee. However, soon Jess begins to learn the truth of the Library he's always believed in as he witnesses an automaton in the form of a lion kill with abandon.<br /><br />Jess also learns about the lengths the Library will go to stop those such as himself who pose a threat to their power. And that doesn't stop Jess' family from enrolling him in the Library's elite and pricey program that would allow him to enter into employment with the Library and become their spy from the inside.<br /><br />Part Harry Potter, part Hunger Games, Ink and Bone introduces us to the Great Library series and the enrollment class for entry into the Library, but in an alternate world ruled for centuries by the Library. Throughout the book, we follow Jess in a third-person limited perspective as he makes his way through the elimination process of postulants attempting to become either Scholars or Guarda (Library military) of the Library.<br /><br />If you've read my reviews before, you know I'm a sucker for these kinds of books. Throw a protagonist in a difficult, nigh on impossible school setting and you already have me halfway. <br /><br />What's great about this entering class is that because of the Library's almost total control, the class students are from all over the world, as diverse as can be, whether from the Middle East, German, or the States. They have an instructor from Hell who has to winnow the class from dozens to 6 ... if he even accepts that many. And the class falls fast.<br /><br />There are only a couple moments I found my disbelief difficult to suspend, because once you find out the volumes are available to anyone on what is termed a "blank," which is essentially an eReader, all we're really fighting about are original volumes of text. They're cool and all, but if you have the knowledge that's the important thing. And apparently they have some type of decent technology so it's difficult to see how much the Library has really held society back.<br /><br />I think the story loses the point a little bit, but focuses back up to show the Library is also preventing knowledge from spreading to the point of murder. And they will do anything to stop threats to their power.<br /><br />I don't read a lot of YA, but I found Ink and Bone to be hugely entertaining. From the very first page, I was enthralled, I couldn't put it down. Yes, I had some moments I questioned, but for pure entertainment value, I was behind this book 100%. <br /><br />I can't recommend Ink and Bone enough. It's a unique world that draws from our own, only if the Library had risen to power and continued to control the world to this day. I had a blast in it and I can't believe I have to wait a whole year for book 2. <br /><br />4 out of 5 Stars (highly recommended)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17380499944433322909" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2011953694" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2011953694" />
    <a title="Heidi The Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7986781-heidi-the-reader"><img alt="Heidi The Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593309467p2/7986781.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2011953694?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heidi The Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heidi The Reader" href="/user/show/7986781-heidi-the-reader">Heidi The Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=fantasy-and-sci-fi">fantasy-and-sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2011953694" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14780197071250484773">In <i>Ink and Bone</i>, knowledge and power is the name of the game.<br/><br/><i>"The Library holds itself to be the keeper of both knowledge and wisdom, but it is not true. So much should never be held in the hands of so few, for it is a natural, venal habit of men to hold to power. And knowledge is the purest form of power."</i> pg 51<br/><br/>Printed books, called originals, are now highly prized and illegal to own without a dispensation from the Library. The Library is an entity without borders as powerful as the church or a</span>
  <span id="freeText14780197071250484773" style="display:none">In <i>Ink and Bone</i>, knowledge and power is the name of the game.<br /><br /><i>"The Library holds itself to be the keeper of both knowledge and wisdom, but it is not true. So much should never be held in the hands of so few, for it is a natural, venal habit of men to hold to power. And knowledge is the purest form of power."</i> pg 51<br /><br />Printed books, called originals, are now highly prized and illegal to own without a dispensation from the Library. The Library is an entity without borders as powerful as the church or a country, with soldiers and animated machines called automatons, protecting its buildings, holdings and librarians.<br /><br />Not everyone follows the Library's restrictions and a black market has formed for books. Jess and his family of smugglers runs and sells books at great threat to life and limb. Other factions also resist the Library. They're called Burners and they destroy books with Greek fire, a dangerous and deadly concoction that burns flesh as easily as paper.<br /><br /><i>"The original scroll had been destroyed by a Burner at the Alexandrian Library ages ago, but there had been one copy made. ... Owning it carried a death penalty. When you steal a book, you steal from the world, the Library propaganda said, and Jess supposed it might be true."</i> pg 22, ebook.<br /><br />Jess' smuggler father decides that he needs eyes and ears on the inside of the most powerful institute in the world, so he arranges an opportunity for Jess to join the Library. And that is where this story really begins.<br /><br />The beginning of <i>Ink and Bone</i> bothered me because of its obvious parallels to <i>Harry Potter</i>. A promising young boy on his way to a magical school boards a train and meets a slightly bumbling, shy boy and the smartest girl in his class. But after that cliche "train introduction", the story improves.<br /><br />While reading this story, I was reminded of the divide between those who love holding traditional books in their hands and ebook readers. The Library has discovered a magical method to use tablets and change the words on the page, very similar to ebooks: <i>"Do you agree it should be wrong to own original works?" Of course, Jess knew he ought to say; it was the standard answer. The Library was never wrong. But something made him say, "I'm not sure." That woke a glint in Wolfe's eyes. "Why not?" "I'd like to hold one," Jess said, quite honestly. "To feel the weight and history of it in my hands. A blank can't be the same, sir." "No," Wolfe agreed. "A blank is a poor, pale imitation, though the words are arranged in precisely the same order; it is the difference between an idea and a physical thing."</i> pg 61, ebook. I enjoy both books and ebooks, but I can see why a reader would prefer one over another.<br /><br />I enjoyed the general ideas of this book, but between the warring factions, actual wars, magic, alchemy, Library history, twin brother, character backgrounds, book burners or eaters, teenage romance and angst, the story lost its cohesiveness. Caine could have written three different stories with the material contained in one.<br /><br />Beyond simplifying the story elements, I just couldn't get over the fact that the librarians weren't good guys. Yes, I'm biased. :) But every librarian I've ever known has been a guardian of knowledge, not gate-keeping tyrants.<br /><br />Recommended for readers who enjoy their young adult fantasy a little scattered and who are open to the idea of sinister librarian-types.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14780197071250484773" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1321953534" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1321953534" />
    <a title="Justine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18656418-justine"><img alt="Justine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588653801p2/18656418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1321953534?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justine" href="/user/show/18656418-justine">Justine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780749017279" href="/book/show/25889417-ink-and-bone">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18656418-justine?shelf=2015-read">2015-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18656418-justine?shelf=favourites-2015">favourites-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1321953534" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5431241952391620516">I absolutely LOVED this adventure book about...books!<br/><br/>Ink and Bone is set in an alternate future where all knowledge in the form of books are controlled by a central authority, <s>(Amazon)</s> The Great Library. <s>(Amazon)</s> The Library doesn’t want anyone else to have original copies of books and basically has it’s own private army of live people and automatons to enforce that. <br/><br/>People are allowed to read anything <s>(Amazon)</s> The Library owns, by way of a copy which is <s>(downloaded)</s> mirrored via alchemy into a </span>
  <span id="freeText5431241952391620516" style="display:none">I absolutely LOVED this adventure book about...books!<br /><br />Ink and Bone is set in an alternate future where all knowledge in the form of books are controlled by a central authority, <s>(Amazon)</s> The Great Library. <s>(Amazon)</s> The Library doesn’t want anyone else to have original copies of books and basically has it’s own private army of live people and automatons to enforce that. <br /><br />People are allowed to read anything <s>(Amazon)</s> The Library owns, by way of a copy which is <s>(downloaded)</s> mirrored via alchemy into a <s>(kindle)</s> blank book. However, since it has a lock on the original books, and you can only read anything using a <s>(kindle)</s> blank book which <s>(Amazon)</s> The Library can erase at any time, even if you have a <s>(kindle)</s> blank copy of a book in your possession it doesn’t really belong to you. Not really. That’s because the <s>(kindles)</s> blanks are <s>(programmed)</s> mirrored using this <s>(proprietary file format including DRM)</s> alchemical process that prevents you from being able to do anything to the copies unless you are a <s>(hacker)</s> Obscurist.<br /><br />Because of their special talent, <s>(hackers)</s> Obscurists are rounded up early by <s>(Amazon)</s> The Library and locked in the Iron Tower, in order to further the interests of that great institution of knowledge and power. Does it sound a bit like absolute power corrupting? Yes indeed.<br /><br />But don’t worry, there are many who feel that the time has come for <s>(Amazon’s)</s> The Library’s tyranny to end. Excitement abounds.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5431241952391620516" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1438717274" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1438717274" />
    <a title="Candi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3639005-candi"><img alt="Candi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585187464p2/3639005.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1438717274?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candi" href="/user/show/3639005-candi">Candi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780451472397" href="/book/show/23398607-ink-and-bone">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3639005-candi?shelf=winter-mini-challenge-2015-2016">winter-mini-challenge-2015-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3639005-candi?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3639005-candi?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3639005-candi?shelf=book-i-own">book-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3639005-candi?shelf=group-read">group-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3639005-candi?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3639005-candi?shelf=snakesandladders">snakesandladders</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1438717274" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2608173957106361303">3.5 stars<br/><br/><i>"The first purpose of a librarian is to preserve and defend our books. Sometimes, that means dying for them - or making someone else die for them. Tota est scientia. Knowledge is all."</i><br/><br/>Imagine what it would be like if you couldn't legally own a single book that you could cherish, re-read over and over again until the pages are dog-eared, and then place it lovingly on your home bookshelf. What if every single word that you read was controlled by a higher power? As readers and book-lovers,</span>
  <span id="freeText2608173957106361303" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br /><br /><i>"The first purpose of a librarian is to preserve and defend our books. Sometimes, that means dying for them - or making someone else die for them. Tota est scientia. Knowledge is all."</i><br /><br />Imagine what it would be like if you couldn't legally own a single book that you could cherish, re-read over and over again until the pages are dog-eared, and then place it lovingly on your home bookshelf. What if every single word that you read was controlled by a higher power? As readers and book-lovers, I don't think we could envision or tolerate such a world! But, that is exactly the world that author Rachel Caine has created for us in the first book in The Great Library series, <b>Ink and Bone</b>. An alternate history where The Great Library of Alexandria was never destroyed but still exists, the invention of the printing press was never allowed to come to fruition, and the librarians and those in higher positions are in absolute control of all dissemination of knowledge through use of a Codex, an electronic means of communication - these are all realities for Jess Brightwell and the myriad cast of characters we come across in this book. The Brightwell family runs an illegal but lucrative business running and selling original books. But then Jess is presented with the opportunity to train and possibly earn a position within the Library itself. He travels from his hometown of London to the glorious city of Alexandria and is joined by a group of postulants from around the world. There begins their difficult and dangerous education under the tutelage of the enigmatic Scholar Wolfe.<br /><br />I have to admit, initially I felt disappointed after the first chapter or two. I was confused about the alternate history – especially the reasoning behind it. I also had trouble figuring out the various roles and hierarchy of the library personnel. Many characters appeared and disappeared rather quickly. It took me to almost the halfway point of this book to really grasp and become interested in this mystifying world. Once everything began to click for me, I was committed to seeing this through to the end. I enjoyed the complexities of some of the characters – in particular, Jess Brightwell, who loves books and wants to do the right thing, despite not always knowing what that might be. Scholar Wolfe grew on me and I would like to hear more of his story. Members of a resistance group, known as the Burners, were intriguing –they were presented as the "bad guys" but is there more to them than meets the eye as well? I suspect I would need to read the next book in the series to find out the answer to that question. <br /><br />There is a lot of peril and adventure in this book, and I found that I turned the pages rather quickly during the second half. I could have done without the magical/alchemy element in this novel – it seems that there were way too many things going on and this just added to the confusion. We also get a glimpse of a war going on between the English and the Welsh, social injustices and starvation of the "common" people, and general unrest – but without a clear explanation as to the origins of this instability. Maybe less is more, at least for me as a reader, but others may find that all these components add to the excitement and intricacies of the plot. <br /><br />I would be interested in reading the sequel with the hope that many unanswered questions will become clearer in my mind. I want to find out what happens next – what does the future hold for Jess and his friends and Scholar Wolfe? Can the library maintain its power? Will the book-lovers of the world someday be able to hold an original book in their hands without fear of punishment? I recommend <b>Ink and Bone</b> to anyone interested in fantasy/alternate history and in particular to fans of fast-paced, young adult novels. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2608173957106361303" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please">Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤  by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=could-read-over-and-over-again">could-read-over-and-over-again</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=serious-cliffhanger">serious-cliffhanger</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1328302072" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10443062173860326683">*4.5* stars<br/><br/><br/><b>
  <i>Give in. Give up.<br/>Survive.</i>
</b><br/><br/><br/><b>Beautiful</b>. <b>Mesmerizing</b>. <b>Addictive</b>. So many words come to mind when I think of this story. I have many regrets as of late, and not being able to read my dystopian/sci-fi/fantasy is one of them. But perhaps the larger crime is that when I do attempt to stick one of these stories in my reading schedule I'm either:<br/><br/>A) too tired<br/>B) too tired <br/>C) too tired <br/><br/>Oh, and did I mention my time has been severely limited? I've always been that girl that scoffs when people sa</span>
  <span id="freeText10443062173860326683" style="display:none">*4.5* stars<br><br><br><b>
  <i>Give in. Give up.<br>Survive.</i>
</b><br><br><br><b>Beautiful</b>. <b>Mesmerizing</b>. <b>Addictive</b>. So many words come to mind when I think of this story. I have many regrets as of late, and not being able to read my dystopian/sci-fi/fantasy is one of them. But perhaps the larger crime is that when I do attempt to stick one of these stories in my reading schedule I'm either:<br><br>A) too tired<br>B) too tired <br>C) too tired <br><br>Oh, and did I mention my time has been severely limited? I've always been that girl that scoffs when people say they are 'too tired' or 'don't have time'. I mean, we have the time we make, ya know? And believe me, I still live by this. I set aside <b>adequate time</b> to read this story, only to realize that after about 10 pages (at times while reading) I wouldn't even know what had happened. That was when I decided it was time to set this story down and pick it up when I had time. <br><br>Doing this pained me-I never put aside those I truly cherish, and this story was just <b>magnificent</b>. But when you can't do it...<u>you just can't fucking do it</u>. So, as I read 50% on Saturday, I decided to read the last 50% (the most action-packed, heart-wrenching parts of the story) when I had the chance. And oh man, did it kill me-what if when I picked it up, the characters/pace/plot were like strangers to me? But as I (surprisingly) gained a large amount of time yesterday, I picked this story up and it was like I'd never left.<br><br><br><b>"No, it's alright," he said, and tried to sit up, but the brief nap had stiffened his sore muscles, and it was a clumsy process. He grabbed at the robe to keep it more or less closed. It was mostly a failed attempt, and it exposed the livid black-and-blue of his side. She took in a breath and came to help him rise. He yanked the robe back together and tied it shut. <br>"Don't apologize," she said. "I've seen worse."<br>"You mean the bruises, I hope."</b><br><br><br>It speaks volumes to me when I can put a story down and come back to it with much (if not all) the same feels. Jess's story intrigued and delighted me, making me feel like I was in this magical world that has long since been lost to me. Dare I say that this reminded me of a very twisted version of <i>Harry Potter</i> mixed with <i>The Testing</i>? Not one moment was dull and more than once I felt like I was trapped in a super psycho version of Hogwarts. <br><br><br><b>Reset the board and keep playing.</b><br><br><br>That's not to say I felt the story was anything like Harry's, naturally. No, what we have here is <b>dark</b>, <b>sinister</b>, and <b>twisted</b>-wrapped in a neat little package so people believe the Library is good, whole, looking out for the betterment of the world and those who wish to prosper in it. But what lies beneath is much more terrifying (Cue <i>The Testing</i> vibes) and unlike anything Jess could have imagined.<br><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/tumblr_mftv2hFCaA1ric07zo1_400_zpsiicc9n1b.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1436884872ra/15514529.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_mftv2hFCaA1ric07zo1_400_zpsiicc9n1b.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><br>What if all you had ever worked for, everything you dreamed of, everything you put your whole life into turned out to be exactly what the underbelly of the world said it was? What if your life's goal turned out to be like making a deal with the devil? And what happens when all of your newly found friends began to disappear in horrible and unimaginable ways.....and not just when they get sent home? What then?<br><br><br><b>What would that be like, to have that single, unshakable faith in the world, to not see all the shadows?</b><br><br><br>Jess was a truly remarkable character. I remember when my lovely friend Anna was talking about him-She got the vibe that he cared more about this futuristic world where books were coveted holier and more valuable than human lives. She wanted him to <i>care</i>, to fight for people. And in a way I see what she's saying-He was kind of out for himself, ya know? But then here's me, right where I always am: <b>Team Boy</b>. I mean, come on. He's a book smuggler, brought up in an illegal business only to pass a test to be admitted for the chance to become a Library Scholar/Representative/Whatever. He is against other students and time and again proves how cunning he is....and yes, he rocks a 'tude....and I fucking loved it. <br><br>Jess is smart and he knows it. He does what he has to to move onto the next round, doing what must be done to move on....but he begins to change. He starts to <i>care</i>. Those people he looked at with competition in his eyes start to become his family, these people who are standing in his way. And would you be so quick to befriend those who could possibly send you back to the horrible world you once lived in? I think not. But Jess...Hmm I loved Jess. Shocking, isn't it?<br><br><br><br><b>
  <i>You said stay.</i>
</b><br><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/greatgats8_zpsvnoi2bny.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1436884915ra/15514536.gif" alt=" photo greatgats8_zpsvnoi2bny.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>And the romance. Daaawww I loved it. While not the main plot point, it still touched me deeply and ripped my heart in two. Morgan and Jess's journey was a tremulous one, danger and secrets swirling around them like an unkempt tornado of peril and destruction. I think that was my favorite part about their romance-which is sick-but I've never said I'm sane, k? <b>Desperation</b>, <b>despair</b>, and <b>longing</b> convolute what <b>is</b>, making for an emotional vortex that you don't realize you're being sucked into....until <b>a plea and raspy voice</b> (Have I mentioned raspy voices in books are my downfall in an emotional scene?? Muaha) are staring you right in the face and you just know it's going to haunt your dreams long after you've finished and gone to bed.<br><br><br><b>He wanted to laugh at himself for being so stupid. He wanted to scream until his throat bled.</b><br><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/tumblr_m4gjkdgaJp1r3rcd2_zpsblbxbz5y.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1436885122ra/15514571.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_m4gjkdgaJp1r3rcd2_zpsblbxbz5y.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>I just...I can't say why I loved this so much. And I can't say I gave it my all-which breaks my heart. A 5 star book has been lowered because, again, I didn't have the time to give to it, so I can assure you I will be re-reading this as soon as humanly possible. Jess's turmoil touched something deep inside of me, and I longed for him to succeed, to break away from the horrible life he grew up living. I am a sucker for male POVs....and I'm more than certain I will be searching for more male POV books-they seem to be my favorites lately. Again, shocking, isn't it?<br><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="200" width="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491628712i/22430034._SX540_.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>
  <b></b>
</u><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea/%20" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="60" width="139" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409285880i/10960212.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>
  <b></b>
